By always using the same notebook for making quick notes, always extracting the main ideas from a text in the same way and always turning them into the same kind of permanent notes, which are always dealt with in the same manner, the number of decisions during a work session can be greatly reduced. ^68iMy2TJ

Externalized notes ^ulLnkxmF

While those who multitasked felt more productive, their productivity actually decreased – a lot ^lA5wHjsd

A lack of structure makes it much more challenging to stay focused for extended periods of time ^vpjVjCdl

Not multitasking, but atomic actions ^xcxrN0fR

- What kind of answer can I expect from asking a question in this 
  particular way? What is missing?
- What is not meant, what is excluded if a certain claim is made?
- What does this all mean for the questions I think about in my slip-box?
- What is so relevant about this thing I am reading/watching/listening 
  to, that it is worth noting down?
- Why did the aspects I wrote down catch my interest?
- What is not in the picture?
- Ask counterfactual questions, like “What if?”. e.g.: It is easier to 
  learn about the function of money in a society if we wonder how 
  strangers would exchange goods without using money. ^ydYRZt8Z

Permanent notes ^q8wUYV5d

Permanent Notes ^r1PU6B6h

Look for
- dis-confirming data
- opposing views
- information that contradicts, corrects,
  supports or adds to what you already have ^aAUlcsEX

Extracting the gist of a text or an idea and giving an account in writing is for academics what daily practice on the piano is for pianists ^7NKS5IWE

Being able to re-frame questions, assertions and information is even more important than having an extensive knowledge, because without this ability, we wouldn’t be able to put our knowledge to use. ^0nTYtzrJ

Writing a summary is a way to confront ourselves when we do not understand something as well as we would like to believe. ^YUz4LwpA

Learning is understanding.
We can only improve our learning if we test ourselves on our progress. ^h9PaILIt

A common way to embed an idea into the context of the slip-box is by writing out the reasons of its importance for your own lines of thought. ^sDXfSF06

Studying, done properly, is research, because it is about gaining insight that cannot be anticipated. If writing is the medium of research, and studying is research, then there is no reason not to work as if nothing else counts but writing. ^flCaKj7l

Compounding interest ^rNO73PUT

A very important feature of a ZK system is the hierarchical nature of note sequences. You should be able to pull out a sequence of notes that contain ideas building on one another, taking an idea deeper and deeper.

You can visually notice cluster of ideas by observing the length of the sequences. ^vg8XvvFZ

A good way to kickstart your ZK is doing a brain dump of your current interests and noting down some foundational ideas you have on those.

Keep it simple. Don't let yourself be distracted by technology options. Use the tool you are familiar with.

Do not spend huge effort on reworking old notes! ^g3mWgORw

Permanent notes are written in the context of your existing notes, following a trail of thought and reflecting/referencing other permanent notes in your system. ^aNaPmuMh

Writing is not a chore, but part of the thinking process. You could argue that writing IS thinking. ^42gMkEiD

- Everything is a permanent note: DILUTION
- Everything is a project note: Always back to square one
- Everything is a fleeting note: Vicious cycle of growing pile
  of notes followed by clear-the-house campaigns ^HHadDDMq

Getting started ^xErPfxbh

Keep it atomic - one idea per note ^HnCIzYnZ

Follow the path of least resistance. Always work on the projects and tasks that are most important to you in the moment. The ZK workflow will ensure all the pieces fall into place. ^THbT7rvS

Planning is a myth, real discoveries are always unexpected, by definition cannot be planned ^Z7rDSi7Z

Deciding on a research topic before having done the research will lead to conflict as most certainly during the work unexpected details will emerge, however due to time pressure there will be a conflict of interest between following the topic and completing the paper based on the original (now irrelevant or misguided) topic. ^9x6J0pc7

The emergent approach is superior! ^JSJMkNpE

To write a good paper, you just need to 
rewrite a good draft

To have a good draft, you just need to 
turn a series notes into continuous text

A series of notes is just the rearrangement of notes you already have in your slip-box

Thus all you really need to do is have a pen in your hand when you read [[HtTSN - Literature Notes#^1141| ]] ^M9t21xG9
